67→def load_class_names(model_path: str) -> dict[int, str]:\\n    68→    \\\"\\\"\\\"Load class names from a JSON file alongside the ONNX model.\\n    69→\\n    70→    Checks for:\\n    71→      1. _nms_iou(boxes: list[dict], iou_thresh: float = NMS_IOU_THRESHOLD) -> list[dict]:\\n   124→    \\\"\\\"\\\"Simple IoU-based NMS for YOLOv8 output.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n   125→    if not boxes:\\n   126→        return boxes\\n   127→    boxes.sort(key=lambda d: d[\\\"confidence\\\"], reverse=True)\\n   128→    keep = []\\n   129→    for box in boxes:\\n   130→        b = box[\\\"bbox\\\"]\\n   131→        bx1 = b[\\\"cx\\\"] - b[\\\"w\\\"] / 2\\n   132→        by1 = b[\\\"cy\\\"] - b[\\\"h\\\"] / 2\\n   133→        bx2 = b[\\\"cx\\\"] + b[\\\"w\\\"] / 2\\n   134→        by2 = b[\\\"cy\\\"] + b[\\\"h\\\"] / 2\\n   135→        overlap = False\\n   136→        for kept in keep:\\n   137→            k = kept[\\\"bbox\\\"]\\n   138→            kx1 = k[\\\"cx\\\"] - k[\\\"w\\\"] / 2\\n   139→            ky1 = k[\\\"cy\\\"] - k[\\\"h\\\"] / 2\\n   140→            kx2 = k[\\\"cx\\\"] + k[\\\"w\\\"] / 2\\n   141→            ky2 = k[\\\"cy\\\"] + k[\\\"h\\\"] / 2\\n   142→            ix1 = max(bx1, kx1)\\n   143→            iy1 = max(by1, ky1)\\n   144→            ix2 = min(bx2, kx2)\\n   145→            iy2 = min(by2, ky2)\\n   146→            inter = max(0, ix2 - ix1) * max(0, iy2 - iy1)\\n   147→            area_b = (bx2 - bx1) * (by2 - by1)\\n   148→            area_k = (kx2 - kx1) * (ky2 - ky1)\\n   149→            union = area_b + area_k - inter\\n   150→            if union > 0 and inter / union > iou_thresh:\\n   151→                overlap = True\\n   152→                break\\n   153→        if not overlap:\\n   154→            keep.append(box)\\n   155→    return keep[:MAX_DETECTIONS_PER_FRAME]\\n   156→\\n   157→\\n   158→def postprocess_yolov8(output: np.ndarray, conf_thresh: float) -> list[dict]:\\n   159→    \\\"\\\"\\\"Parse YOLOv8 output [1, 84, 8400] -> list of detections with NMS.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n   160→    preds = output[0].T  # [8400, 84]\\n   161→    detections = []\\n   162→\\n   163→    for pred in preds:\\n   164→        box = pred[:4]\\n   165→        class_scores = pred[4:]\\n   166→        max_score = float(np.max(class_scores))\\n   167→        if max_score < conf_thresh:\\n   168→            continue\\n   169→\\n   170→        class_id = int(np.argmax(class_scores))\\n   171→        cx, cy, w, h = box\\n   172→        detections.append({\\n   173→            \\\"class_id\\\": class_id,\\n   174→            \\\"confidence\\\": round(max_score, 4),\\n   175→            \\\"bbox\\\": {\\n   176→                \\\"cx\\\": round(float(cx) / INPUT_SIZE, 4),\\n   177→                \\\"cy\\\": round(float(cy) / INPUT_SIZE, 4),\\n   178→                \\\"w\\\": round(float(w) / INPUT_SIZE, 4),\\n   179→                \\\"h\\\": round(float(h) / INPUT_SIZE, 4),\\n   180→            },\\n   181→        })\\n   182→\\n   183→    return _nms_iou(detections)\\n   184→\\n   185→\\n   186→def postprocess_nms_free(output: np.ndarray, conf_thresh: float) -> list[dict]:\\n   187→    \\\"\\\"\\\"Parse YOLO26 NMS-free output [1, 300, 6] -> list of detections.\\n   188→\\n   189→    Each row: [x1, y1, x2, y2, score, class_id] in pixel coords.\\n   190→    No NMS needed — model handles it end-to-end.\\n   191→    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n   192→    preds = output[0]  # [300, 6]\\n   193→    detections = []\\n   194→\\n   195→    for pred in preds:\\n   196→        x1, y1, x2, y2, score, class_id = pred\\n   197→        # YOLO26 scores may be raw logits — apply sigmoid to normalize to 0.0-1.0\\n   198→        if score > 1.0:\\n   199→            score = 1.0 / (1.0 + np.exp(-score))  # sigmoid\\n   200→        if score < conf_thresh:\\n   201→            continue\\n   202→\\n   203→        cx = (x1 + x2) / 2.0\\n   204→        cy = (y1 + y2) / 2.0\\n   205→        w = x2 - x1\\n   206→        h = y2 - y1\\n   207→\\n   208→        detections.append({\\n   209→            \\\"class_id\\\": int(class_id),\\n   210→            \\\"confidence\\\": round(float(score), 4),\\n   211→            \\\"bbox\\\": {\\n   212→                \\\"cx\\\": round(float(cx) / INPUT_SIZE, 4),\\n   213→                \\\"cy\\\": round(float(cy) / INPUT_SIZE, 4),\\n   214→                \\\"w\\\": round(float(w) / INPUT_SIZE, 4),\\n   215→                \\\"h\\\": round(float(h) / INPUT_SIZE, 4),\\n   216→            },\\n   217→        })\\n   218→\\n   219→    detections.sort(key=lambda d: d[\\\"confidence\\\"], reverse=True)\\n   220→    return detections[:MAX_DETECTIONS_PER_FRAME]\\n   221→\\n   222→\\n   223→def postprocess_custom_export(output: np.ndarray, conf_thresh: float, session=None) -> list[dict]:\\n   224→    \\\"\\\"\\\"Parse custom ONNX export output -- auto-detects format.\\n   225→\\n   226→    Custom-trained models exported as YOLOv8 produce [1, 4+C, N] (same return True\n    43→\n    44→\n    45→def _record_success(channel: str) -> None:\n    46→    _circuit_breakers[channel][\"failures\"] = 0\n    47→\n    48→\n    49→def _record_failure(channel: str) -> 139→def _send_smtp_email(config: dict, to_email: str, subject: str, body_html: str) -> bool:\n   140→    \"\"\"Send an email via SMTP using decrypted config.\"\"\"\n   141→    import smtplib\n   142→ 551→async def push_config(\n   552→    body: dict,\n   553→    agent: dict = Depends(get_edge_agent),\n   554→    db: AsyncIOMotorDatabase = Depends(get_db),\n   555→):\n   556→    # Validate: only 575→@router.post(\"/sync/incidents\")\n   576→async def sync_incidents_from_edge(\n   577→    body: dict,\n   578→    request: Request,\n   579→    agent: dict = Depends(get_edge_agent),\n   580→    db: AsyncIOMotorDatabase = Depends(get_db),\n   581→):\n   582→    \"\"\"Receive batch of incidents created on edge for cloud storage.\n   583→\n   584→    Edge sends complete incident objects with grouped detections.\n   585→    Cloud creates/merges into events collection and triggers notifications.\n   586→    \"\"\"\n   587→    org_id = agent[\"org_id\"]\n   588→    store_id = agent.get(\"store_id\", \"\")\n   589→\n   590→    incidents = body.get(\"incidents\", [])\n   591→    synced_ids: list[str] = []\n   592→    errors: list[str] = []\n   593→\n   594→    for inc in incidents:\n   595→        try:\n   596→            edge_id = inc.get(\"id\", \"\")\n   597→            camera_name = inc.get(\"camera_id\", \"\")\n   598→\n   599→            # Resolve camera name to UUID\n   600→            camera = await db.cameras.find_one({\"name\": camera_name, \"store_id\": store_id})\n   601→            camera_id = camera[\"id\"] if camera else camera_name\n   602→\n   603→            # Check if already synced (by edge_incident_id OR by camera+time window)\n   604→            existing = await db.events.find_one({\"edge_incident_id\": edge_id, \"org_id\": org_id})\n   605→            now = datetime.now(timezone.utc)\n   606→\n   607→            # Also check for cloud-created incident from frame upload (same camera, open, same time window)\n   608→            if not existing and inc.get(\"start_time\"):\n   609→                try:\n   610→                    edge_start = datetime.fromisoformat(inc[\"start_time\"])\n   611→                    if edge_start.tzinfo is None:\n   612→                        edge_start = edge_start.replace(tzinfo=timezone.utc)\n   613→                    from datetime import timedelta\n   614→                    window_start = edge_start - timedelta(seconds=settings.INCIDENT_DEDUP_WINDOW_SECONDS)\n   615→                    existing = await db.events.find_one({\n   616→                        \"org_id\": org_id,\n   617→                        \"camera_id\": camera_id,\n   618→                        \"status\": {\"$in\": [\"new\", \"acknowledged\"]},\n   619→                        \"start_time\": {\"$gte\": window_start},\n   620→                        \"edge_incident_id\": {\"$exists\": False},\n   621→                    }, sort=[(\"start_time\", -1)])\n   622→                    if existing:\n   623→                        # Link cloud incident to edge incident for future merges\n   624→                        await db.events.update_one(\n   625→                            {\"id\": existing[\"id\"]},\n   626→                            {\"$set\": {\"edge_incident_id\": edge_id}},\n   627→                        )\n   628→                except Exception:\n   629→                    pass\n   630→\n   631→            if existing:\n   632→                # Merge: update if edge has more detections\n   633→                edge_count = inc.get(\"detection_count\", 1)\n   634→                if edge_count > existing.get(\"detection_count\", 0):\n   635→                    await db.events.update_one(\n   636→                        {\"id\": existing[\"id\"]},\n   637→                        {\"$set\": {\n   638→                            \"detection_count\": edge_count,\n   639→                            \"max_confidence\": max(existing.get(\"max_confidence\", 0), inc.get(\"max_confidence\", 0)),\n   640→                            \"max_wet_area_percent\": max(existing.get(\"max_wet_area_percent\", 0), inc.get(\"max_wet_area_percent\", 0)),\n   641→                            \"severity\": inc.get(\"severity\", existing.get(\"severity\")),\n   642→                            \"end_time\": inc.get(\"end_time\") or existing.get(\"end_time\"),\n   643→                            \"status\": inc.get(\"status\", existing.get(\"status\")),\n   644→                            \"updated_at\": now,\n   645→                        }},\n   646→                    )\n   647→                synced_ids.append(edge_id)\n   648→            else:\n   649→                # Create new event from edge incident\n   650→                event_id = str(uuid.uuid4())\n {"parentUuid":"e013ea46-dea7-4162-bbb5-5d3f7487a78d","isSidechain":true,"agentId":"a64034d4101c43c17","message":{"model":"claude-opus-4-6","id":"msg_01EA1D7A8bbyaTi1YfD9vGMK","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"text","text":"I now have a comprehensive understanding of the system. Here is the complete structured design audit.\n\n---\n\n# FloorEye v2.0 Design Audit Report\n\n---\n\n## ROLE 1: SYSTEM ARCHITECT FINDINGS\n\n### SA-01: Single MongoDB Instance is a Single Point of Failure\n\n- **Diagram**: ARCHITECTURE (infrastructure layer)\n- **Description**: Both `docker-compose.dev.yml` and `docker-compose.prod.yml` run a single MongoDB 7.0 instance with no replication. All services (backend, worker, edge sync) depend on it. If MongoDB goes down, the entire platform is dead -- no detections, no incidents, no auth.\n- **Root Cause**: No MongoDB replica set configured; single container deployment.\n- **Impact**: Total platform outage. All detection data in-flight is lost. Edge agents buffer locally but cloud dashboard is blind.\n- **Severity**: CRITICAL\n- **Solution**: Deploy MongoDB as a 3-node replica set (primary + 2 secondaries). Use `mongos` or direct replica set connection string. For production, use MongoDB Atlas or a managed service.\n- **Priority**: 1\n\n### SA-02: Single Redis Instance is a Single Point of Failure\n\n- **Diagram**: ARCHITECTURE (infrastructure layer)\n- **Description**: Redis 7.2 runs as a single instance serving rate limiting, Celery broker, Celery result backend, and WebSocket pub/sub. No Redis Sentinel or Cluster.\n- **Root Cause**: Single container, no HA configuration.\n- **Impact**: If Redis dies: rate limiting falls back to per-worker in-memory (inconsistent limits), Celery tasks stop processing, WebSocket broadcasts fail (silently falls back to local-only), all queued tasks are lost.\n- **Severity**: CRITICAL\n- **Solution**: Deploy Redis Sentinel (3 nodes) or Redis Cluster. Alternatively, use managed Redis (AWS ElastiCache, Upstash). For Celery, consider using a dedicated broker (RabbitMQ) separate from cache Redis.\n- **Priority**: 2\n\n### SA-03: No API Gateway or Load Balancer\n\n- **Diagram**: ARCHITECTURE (network layer)\n- **Description**: Nginx serves as a simple reverse proxy with no load balancing across multiple backend instances. The `docker-compose.prod.yml` runs a single backend with 4 Gunicorn workers. Cloudflare Tunnel connects directly to the web container.\n- **Root Cause**: Single-container deployment model with no horizontal scaling.\n- **Impact**: Cannot scale horizontally. A single backend process handles all API traffic, WebSocket connections, and edge agent communication. At 100+ stores with 1000 cameras sending heartbeats every 30s, the backend will saturate.\n- **Severity**: HIGH\n- **Solution**: Deploy behind a load balancer (AWS ALB, Traefik, or HAProxy). Run multiple backend replicas. Use sticky sessions for WebSocket connections or move to a dedicated WebSocket gateway.\n- **Priority**: 3\n\n### SA-04: WebSocket Scalability Bottleneck -- No Connection Limits\n\n- **Diagram**: DATA_FLOW (live monitoring flow)\n- **Description**: The `ConnectionManager` in `websockets.py` stores all WebSocket connections in a Python dict (`_connections`). There are no connection limits per user, per org, or globally. Each live-frame subscription is per-camera, so 1000 cameras with 5 viewers each = 5000 persistent connections on a single process.\n- **Root Cause**: In-memory connection tracking with no resource limits.\n- **Impact**: Memory exhaustion at scale. A single Gunicorn worker holding 1000+ WebSocket connections will consume significant memory and CPU for broadcasts. No backpressure mechanism.\n- **Severity**: HIGH\n- **Solution**: (1) Add max connection limits per user/org. (2) Implement connection pooling. (3) Consider a dedicated WebSocket service (e.g., Centrifugo, Socket.IO with Redis adapter). (4) Add heartbeat/ping-pong to detect stale connections.\n- **Priority**: 4\n\n### SA-05: Celery Workers Share Single Queue (No Priority or Isolation)\n\n- **Diagram**: DATA_FLOW (detection/notification flow)\n- **Description**: Only the detection worker has a dedicated queue (`detection`). Notification tasks (email, SMS, push, webhook) share the default Celery queue with health checks, incident workers, sync workers, and OTA workers. A flood of notifications can starve other task types.\n- **Root Cause**: `task_routes` only defines routing for detection tasks; all others go to default.\n- **Impact**: During a mass incident (e.g., pipe burst flooding 50 cameras simultaneously), notification tasks could overwhelm the queue, delaying health checks and incident auto-close.\n- **Severity**: MEDIUM\n- **Solution**: Define separate queues: `notifications`, `health`, `sync`, `ota`. Run dedicated workers per queue with appropriate concurrency.\n- **Priority**: 5\n\n### SA-06: No Service Discovery for Edge Agents\n\n- **Diagram**: ARCHITECTURE (edge-to-cloud boundary)\n- **Description**: Edge agents connect to the cloud backend via a hardcoded URL. There is no service registry, no health-aware routing, and no failover. If the backend URL changes or goes down, all edge agents lose connectivity.\n- **Root Cause**: Static configuration in edge agent `config.py`.\n- **Impact**: Edge agents continue to buffer locally (good), but cannot sync detections, receive commands, or download model updates until manually reconfigured.\n- **Severity**: MEDIUM\n- **Solution**: Use DNS-based service discovery. Implement edge agent config that supports multiple backend URLs with automatic failover. The Cloudflare Tunnel partially mitigates this but is itself a SPOF.\n- **Priority**: 6\n\n### SA-07: No Caching Layer for Frequently Queried Data\n\n- **Diagram**: DATA_FLOW (detection control resolution)\n- **Description**: Every detection and incident creation calls `resolve_effective_settings()` which performs up to 4 MongoDB queries (org, store, camera, and class overrides). At 1000 cameras running at 2 FPS, this is 8000 MongoDB queries/second just for settings resolution.\n- **Root Cause**: No Redis or in-memory caching of detection control settings.\n- **Impact**: MongoDB becomes the bottleneck. Detection latency increases. Settings are rarely changed but queried on every single frame.\n- **Severity**: HIGH\n- **Solution**: Cache resolved settings in Redis with a TTL of 60 seconds. Invalidate on settings update (publish invalidation event via Redis pub/sub).\n- **Priority**: 3\n\n### SA-08: No Observability Stack (Metrics, Tracing, Log Aggregation)\n\n- **Diagram**: ARCHITECTURE (cross-cutting)\n- **Description**: The system uses Python `logging` to stdout. There is no Prometheus metrics endpoint, no OpenTelemetry tracing, no structured log aggregation (ELK, Loki, CloudWatch). The health check endpoint (`/api/v1/health`) only checks MongoDB and Redis ping.\n- **Root Cause**: Observability was not included in any of the 12 build phases.\n- **Impact**: No visibility into: inference latency distributions, detection throughput, WebSocket connection counts, Celery queue depths, error rates by endpoint, or edge agent fleet health trends. Debugging production issues requires SSH and log tailing.\n- **Severity**: HIGH\n- **Solution**: (1) Add Prometheus client with `/metrics` endpoint. (2) Deploy Grafana for dashboards. (3) Add OpenTelemetry spans on key flows (detection, incident, notification). (4) Ship logs to a centralized system (Loki + Grafana, or CloudWatch).\n- **Priority**: 4\n\n### SA-09: Tight Coupling Between Detection Service and Incident Service\n\n- **Diagram**: DATA_FLOW (detection-to-incident flow)\n- **Description**: `detection_service.py` directly imports and calls `create_or_update_incident()`, `publish_detection()`, `dispatch_notifications()`, and `emit_system_log()` synchronously within the same request path. A failure in any downstream call can affect detection logging.\n- **Root Cause**: Direct function calls instead of event-driven architecture.\n- **Impact**: Notification service failure can slow down detection processing. No ability to replay failed events. Tight coupling makes it hard to scale services independently.\n- **Severity**: MEDIUM\n- **Solution**: Decouple via event bus pattern. After detection is logged, publish a `detection.created` event to Redis/Celery. Separate consumers handle incident creation, notification dispatch, and WebSocket broadcasting independently.\n- **Priority**: 7\n\n### SA-10: Missing Request/Response Size Limits on Edge Frame Uploads\n\n- **Diagram**: DATA_FLOW (edge-to-cloud upload)\n- **Description**: The `/api/v1/edge/frame` endpoint accepts `frame_base64` and `annotated_frame_base64` with no size validation. Nginx has `client_max_body_size 50M`, but a single base64-encoded 4K frame could be 15-25 MB. Edge agents could inadvertently send oversized payloads.\n- **Root Cause**: No request body size validation at the application level.\n- **Impact**: Memory pressure on backend. A burst of large frames can OOM the backend process.\n- **Severity**: MEDIUM\n- **Solution**: Add Pydantic field validators with max length on base64 fields. Set a reasonable limit (e.g., 5 MB per frame). Add request body size middleware.\n- **Priority**: 8\n\n---\n\n## ROLE 2: BACKEND ENGINEER FINDINGS\n\n### BE-01: Celery Workers Create New MongoDB Client Per Task Invocation\n\n- **Diagram**: DATA_FLOW (worker execution)\n- **Description**: Every Celery task (`incident_worker.py`, `notification_worker.py`, `detection_worker.py`) calls `_get_db()` which creates a `new AsyncIOMotorClient(settings.MONGODB_URI)` on every execution. Motor clients maintain connection pools, so creating one per task wastes TCP connections and adds latency.\n- **Root Cause**: No shared connection pool in the Celery worker process. Each task creates and discards a client.\n- **Impact**: Connection churn on MongoDB. At high throughput, could exhaust MongoDB's max connections (default 65536). Each client creation adds ~50-100ms latency.\n- **Severity**: HIGH\n- **Solution**: Create a module-level singleton Motor client per worker process. Use Celery's `worker_process_init` signal to initialize and `worker_process_shutdown` to close.\n- **Priority**: 2\n\n### BE-02: Synchronous Event Loop Creation in Celery Tasks is Fragile\n\n- **Diagram**: DATA_FLOW (worker execution)\n- **Description**: Every Celery task creates a new `asyncio.new_event_loop()`, runs `loop.run_until_complete()`, then closes the loop. This pattern is used in `incident_worker.py`, `notification_worker.py`, `detection_worker.py`, and `health_worker.py`. Multiple nested loop creations (e.g., `_increment_delivery_attempts` inside a retry) can fail.\n- **Root Cause**: Celery is sync-first; async code is wrapped manually.\n- **Impact**: Race conditions with nested loop.run_until_complete calls. Event loop not properly cleaned up on exceptions. Memory leaks from unclosed loops.\n- **Severity**: MEDIUM\n- **Solution**: Use `asgiref.sync.async_to_sync` or the Celery-compatible `celery[asyncio]` integration. Alternatively, use a single event loop per worker process.\n- **Priority**: 5\n\n### BE-03: No Dead Letter Queue for Failed Celery Tasks\n\n- **Diagram**: DATA_FLOW (notification flow)\n- **Description**: Notification tasks have `max_retries=3-5` with exponential backoff. After max retries are exhausted, the task is silently discarded. There is no dead letter queue (DLQ) to capture permanently failed tasks for later investigation.\n- **Root Cause**: No `on_failure` handler or DLQ routing configured in `celery_app.py`.\n- **Impact**: Lost notifications. An SMTP server down for 10 minutes could result in permanently lost email notifications with no record of failure beyond log lines.\n- **Severity**: HIGH\n- **Solution**: Configure a DLQ in Celery (`task_reject_on_worker_lost=True`). Add `on_failure` handlers that write failed task metadata to a `failed_tasks` MongoDB collection. Build an admin UI to retry/inspect failed tasks.\n- **Priority**: 3\n\n### BE-04: No API Versioning Strategy\n\n- **Diagram**: ARCHITECTURE (API layer)\n- **Description**: All routes use `/api/v1/` prefix. There is no plan for `v2` migration, no deprecation headers, and the OpenAPI spec is at `/api/v1/openapi.json`. The edge agents are hardcoded to `v1` endpoints.\n- **Root Cause**: Single version deployed; no versioning middleware.\n- **Impact**: Any breaking API change will require simultaneous updates to all edge agents (which may be offline), the web frontend, and the mobile app. This is particularly dangerous for edge agents that auto-update on their own schedule.\n- **Severity**: MEDIUM\n- **Solution**: Implement content negotiation or URL-based versioning. Support running `v1` and `v2` simultaneously during migration periods. Add `Deprecation` and `Sunset` headers.\n- **Priority**: 9\n\n### BE-05: Detection History Pagination Uses skip/offset (O(n) Performance)\n\n- **Diagram**: ER_DIAGRAM (detection_logs collection)\n- **Description**: `list_detections()` in `detection_service.py` uses `.skip(offset).limit(limit)` for pagination. MongoDB's `skip()` scans and discards documents, making page N cost O(N*limit).\n- **Root Cause**: Standard offset-based pagination pattern.\n- **Impact**: At 1M+ detection logs (realistic for 100 stores over months), accessing page 1000 requires MongoDB to scan 20,000 documents before returning 20. Queries become progressively slower.\n- **Severity**: MEDIUM\n- **Solution**: Implement cursor-based (keyset) pagination using `timestamp` + `id` as the cursor. Replace `skip(offset)` with `{\"timestamp\": {\"$lt\": cursor_timestamp}}`.\n- **Priority**: 6\n\n### BE-06: count_documents() Called Before Every List Query\n\n- **Diagram**: ER_DIAGRAM (multiple collections)\n- **Description**: `list_detections()`, `list_incidents()`, and similar functions call `await db.collection.count_documents(query)` before fetching the actual page. This is a separate full-count query on every page request.\n- **Root Cause**: Standard total-count pattern for pagination metadata.\n- **Impact**: Doubles the MongoDB load for every list endpoint. `count_documents()` on a large collection with a complex filter can take seconds.\n- **Severity**: MEDIUM\n- **Solution**: Use `estimated_document_count()` for unfiltered counts. For filtered counts, use `count_documents()` only on the first page and cache the result. Alternatively, return `has_more: true/false` instead of exact totals.\n- **Priority**: 7\n\n### BE-07: WebSocket Authentication Uses Query Parameter Token (Security Risk)\n\n- **Diagram**: DATA_FLOW (live monitoring flow)\n- **Description**: WebSocket auth passes JWT as `?token=<jwt>` query parameter. This token appears in server access logs, browser history, proxy logs, and potentially in error reporting.\n- **Root Cause**: WebSocket protocol does not support custom headers during handshake in browsers.\n- **Impact**: JWT tokens leaked in logs. Tokens could be captured by intermediate proxies.\n- **Severity**: MEDIUM\n- **Solution**: Use a short-lived, single-use ticket system: client first calls a REST endpoint to get a one-time WebSocket ticket (UUID, expires in 30s), then connects with `?ticket=<uuid>`. The ticket is invalidated on first use.\n- **Priority**: 6\n\n### BE-08: No Idempotency Keys on Edge Frame/Detection Uploads\n\n- **Diagram**: DATA_FLOW (edge-to-cloud upload)\n- **Description**: The `/api/v1/edge/frame` and `/api/v1/edge/detection` endpoints create a new detection log with `uuid.uuid4()` on every call. If an edge agent retries a failed upload (network timeout), the same detection gets logged twice.\n- **Root Cause**: No idempotency mechanism.\n- **Impact**: Duplicate detection logs, inflated detection counts on incidents, double notifications.\n- **Severity**: HIGH\n- **Solution**: Accept an `idempotency_key` from the edge agent (e.g., `{camera_id}:{timestamp}:{hash}`). Check for duplicates before inserting. Return the existing detection if already processed.\n- **Priority**: 4\n\n### BE-09: Health Check Creates New Synchronous Redis Connection Every Call\n\n- **Diagram**: ARCHITECTURE (health endpoint)\n- **Description**: In `main.py`, the `/api/v1/health` endpoint creates a synchronous `redis.from_url()` connection, pings, then closes it -- on every health check call. Load balancers typically poll health every 10-30 seconds, so this creates constant connection churn.\n- **Root Cause**: No persistent Redis connection for health checks.\n- **Impact**: Connection overhead on every health check. If Redis is slow, health checks stack up and timeout.\n- **Severity**: LOW\n- **Solution**: Use the existing async Redis client from the WebSocket module or create a persistent health-check Redis connection.\n- **Priority**: 10\n\n### BE-10: Rate Limiter Key Generation is Inconsistent\n\n- **Diagram**: ARCHITECTURE (middleware layer)\n- **Description**: The rate limiter key is `f\"rl:{client_ip}:{path.split('/')[4]}\"`. This means `/api/v1/stores/abc` and `/api/v1/stores/xyz` share the same rate limit key (both extract `stores`). Different operations on the same resource type are conflated.\n- **Root Cause**: Overly aggressive path normalization.\n- **Impact**: A user listing stores could exhaust the rate limit for creating stores. Rate limiting is per-router-prefix rather than per-endpoint.\n- **Severity**: LOW\n- **Solution**: Use the full path (minus dynamic IDs) or endpoint name as the rate limit key. Better: use a proper rate limiting library like `slowapi` with configurable per-endpoint limits.\n- **Priority**: 8\n\n---\n\n## ROLE 3: DEVOPS / CLOUD ENGINEER FINDINGS\n\n### DO-01: No Container Orchestration (Docker Compose in Production)\n\n- **Diagram**: ARCHITECTURE (deployment layer)\n- **Description**: Production runs on `docker-compose.prod.yml` with 6 containers (backend, worker, web, mongodb, redis, minio) + cloudflared. Docker Compose provides no auto-scaling, no rolling deployments, no self-healing beyond `restart: unless-stopped`.\n- **Root Cause**: No Kubernetes, ECS, or Nomad deployment.\n- **Impact**: Zero downtime deployments are impossible. If the host machine reboots, all services restart simultaneously, potentially causing cascading failures. No horizontal scaling.\n- **Severity**: CRITICAL\n- **Solution**: Migrate to Kubernetes (EKS/GKE/k3s) or AWS ECS. Define deployment manifests with readiness/liveness probes, resource limits, and HPA (Horizontal Pod Autoscaler).\n- **Priority**: 1\n\n### DO-02: MongoDB Has No Authentication in Production\n\n- **Diagram**: ARCHITECTURE (data layer)\n- **Description**: `docker-compose.prod.yml` line 44 explicitly notes: \"MongoDB auth deferred to post-pilot. Requires fresh volume or manual user creation.\" MongoDB runs without `MONGO_INITDB_ROOT_USERNAME/PASSWORD`.\n- **Root Cause**: Auth was deferred and never implemented.\n- **Impact**: Any process that can reach the MongoDB port can read/write/delete all data. On a shared network, this is a data breach waiting to happen. Even with no port exposed, other containers on the Docker network have full access.\n- **Severity**: CRITICAL\n- **Solution**: Enable MongoDB authentication immediately. Create a dedicated application user with minimal privileges. Update `MONGODB_URI` with credentials. Create an init script for fresh deployments.\n- **Priority**: 1\n\n### DO-03: Secrets Stored as Environment Variables and Defaults in Code\n\n- **Diagram**: ARCHITECTURE (security layer)\n- **Description**: `config.py` has hardcoded default secrets: `CHANGE_ME_256_BIT_SECRET`, `CHANGE_ME_EDGE_SECRET`, `CHANGE_ME_BASE64_32_BYTE_KEY`, and `minioadmin`. While production blocks insecure defaults, the Redis password `flooreye_redis_2026` is used as a default in `docker-compose.prod.yml`. Secrets are passed via `.env` files.\n- **Root Cause**: No secret management solution (Vault, AWS Secrets Manager, SOPS).\n- **Impact**: `.env` files can be accidentally committed, leaked in container images, or exposed in container inspect. Redis default password is in plain text in the compose file.\n- **Severity**: HIGH\n- **Solution**: Use Docker secrets, HashiCorp Vault, or AWS Secrets Manager. For Kubernetes migration, use sealed secrets or external-secrets-operator. Remove all default passwords from compose files.\n- **Priority**: 2\n\n### DO-04: No Backup Strategy for MongoDB or MinIO\n\n- **Diagram**: ARCHITECTURE (data layer)\n- **Description**: MongoDB data is on a Docker volume (`mongo_data`). MinIO data is on `minio_data`. There are no backup jobs, no point-in-time recovery, no replication, and no backup verification.\n- **Root Cause**: No backup infrastructure was built.\n- **Impact**: A single `docker volume rm` or disk failure permanently destroys all detection logs, incidents, user accounts, model versions, and stored frames/clips. Complete data loss.\n- **Severity**: CRITICAL\n- **Solution**: (1) Schedule `mongodump` to S3 daily (or use MongoDB Atlas continuous backup). (2) Enable MinIO replication or use AWS S3 directly. (3) Implement backup verification with periodic restore tests. (4) Set up MongoDB oplog for point-in-time recovery.\n- **Priority**: 1\n\n### DO-05: No Log Aggregation or Centralized Logging\n\n- **Diagram**: ARCHITECTURE (observability)\n- **Description**: All services log to stdout/stderr. Docker captures these in JSON log files on the host. There is no ELK stack, no Loki, no CloudWatch, no log rotation configuration.\n- **Root Cause**: Centralized logging was not in scope for any phase.\n- **Impact**: Logs are scattered across 6+ containers. Correlating an edge detection through to notification delivery requires accessing multiple container logs. No log search, no alerting on error patterns. Docker default log driver can fill disk.\n- **Severity**: HIGH\n- **Solution**: Deploy Loki + Grafana (lightweight) or ELK stack. Configure Docker logging driver to ship to the aggregator. Add structured JSON logging with correlation IDs.\n- **Priority**: 3\n\n### DO-06: No Metrics Collection or Alerting\n\n- **Diagram**: ARCHITECTURE (observability)\n- **Description**: No Prometheus, no Grafana, no Datadog, no CloudWatch metrics. The only monitoring is the `/api/v1/health` endpoint and the periodic `health_worker.py` Celery task (which logs to stdout and updates integration configs).\n- **Root Cause**: Monitoring was not in scope.\n- **Impact**: No alerts when: MongoDB is slow, Redis memory is full, Celery queues are backed up, edge agents disconnect en masse, disk is filling, or error rates spike. Issues are only discovered when users report them.\n- **Severity**: HIGH\n- **Solution**: (1) Add Prometheus client to FastAPI with `/metrics`. (2) Deploy Prometheus + Grafana. (3) Set up alerting via PagerDuty or OpsGenie for: error rate > 5%, p99 latency > 2s, Celery queue depth > 100, edge agent offline count > threshold.\n- **Priority**: 3\n\n### DO-07: No Edge Agent Update/Rollback Strategy\n\n- **Diagram**: ARCHITECTURE (edge deployment)\n- **Description**: Edge agents run via Docker Compose on-premise. There is a `command_poller.py` that receives commands from the cloud, and an `ota_worker.py` stub, but no documented update mechanism. If a bad agent version is deployed, there is no automated rollback.\n- **Root Cause**: OTA update system is a stub, not fully implemented.\n- **Impact**: Deploying a buggy edge agent version to 100 stores requires manual SSH intervention to each site. During the outage window, detection stops.\n- **Severity**: HIGH\n- **Solution**: Implement blue-green or canary deployment for edge agents. Use Watchtower or a custom OTA system that: (1) pulls new images, (2) runs health check, (3) automatically rolls back if health check fails. Store previous image tags for instant rollback.\n- **Priority**: 5\n\n### DO-08: No TLS Between Internal Services\n\n- **Diagram**: ARCHITECTURE (network layer)\n- **Description**: Nginx listens on port 80 (no HTTPS). Backend, MongoDB, Redis, and MinIO communicate over unencrypted connections within the Docker network. Cloudflare Tunnel provides external TLS but internal traffic is plain.\n- **Root Cause**: Internal network assumed to be trusted.\n- **Impact**: Any container compromise or network sniffing on the Docker bridge can capture MongoDB queries, Redis commands (including tokens), and API responses in plain text.\n- **Severity**: MEDIUM\n- **Solution**: Enable TLS on MongoDB (`--tlsMode requireTLS`). Enable TLS on Redis (`tls-port`). Use HTTPS between Nginx and backend. For Kubernetes, use a service mesh (Istio/Linkerd) for automatic mTLS.\n- **Priority**: 7\n\n### DO-09: No Container Resource Limits\n\n- **Diagram**: ARCHITECTURE (deployment)\n- **Description**: Neither `docker-compose.dev.yml` nor `docker-compose.prod.yml` defines memory limits, CPU limits, or reservations for any container. The backend Gunicorn timeout is 30s but there are no OOM protections.\n- **Root Cause**: Resource limits were not configured.\n- **Impact**: A memory leak in any container (e.g., accumulating WebSocket connections, unclosed MongoDB clients in Celery workers) can consume all host memory and crash all containers. A CPU-intensive operation (model training, video encoding) can starve other services.\n- **Severity**: HIGH\n- **Solution**: Add `deploy.resources.limits` in compose files. Example: backend 2GB/2CPU, worker 1GB/1CPU, MongoDB 4GB, Redis 512MB. Set `--oom-kill-disable=false`.\n- **Priority**: 4\n\n### DO-10: No CI/CD Pipeline for Edge Agent Deployment\n\n- **Diagram**: ARCHITECTURE (CI/CD)\n- **Description**: GitHub Actions workflows exist for `test.yml`, `deploy-backend.yml`, and `ci.yml`, but there is no pipeline for building and deploying edge agent Docker images. Edge agents are deployed manually.\n- **Root Cause**: Edge deployment automation was not built.\n- **Impact**: Manual edge deployments are error-prone and do not scale. Cannot guarantee consistent versions across sites.\n- **Severity**: MEDIUM\n- **Solution**: Build a CI pipeline that: (1) builds edge agent Docker images on tag, (2) pushes to a container registry (ECR, GHCR), (3) notifies edge agents via the command system to pull the new version.\n- **Priority**: 6\n\n### DO-11: No Disaster Recovery Plan\n\n- **Diagram**: ARCHITECTURE (cross-cutting)\n- **Description**: There is no documented DR plan. No RTO/RPO targets. No secondary region. No tested recovery procedure.\n- **Root Cause**: DR was not scoped in any phase.\n- **Impact**: A host failure, datacenter outage, or ransomware attack results in unknown downtime. Recovery requires manual reconstruction from Docker volumes (if available) and redeployment.\n- **Severity**: HIGH\n- **Solution**: (1) Document RTO/RPO targets. (2) Implement automated backups (see DO-04). (3) Test recovery monthly. (4) For multi-region, replicate MongoDB and use DNS failover. (5) Store infrastructure as code (Terraform/Pulumi).\n- **Priority**: 5\n\n### DO-12: MinIO Uses Default Credentials in Production Compose\n\n- **Diagram**: ARCHITECTURE (storage layer)\n- **Description**: `docker-compose.prod.yml` uses `MINIO_ROOT_USER: ${MINIO_ROOT_USER:-minioadmin}` and `MINIO_ROOT_PASSWORD: ${MINIO_ROOT_PASSWORD:-minioadmin}`. If env vars are not set, MinIO runs with default admin credentials.\n- **Root Cause**: Default fallback values in compose file.\n- **Impact**: Unauthorized access to all stored frames, clips, model files, and annotated images. Data exfiltration or deletion.\n- **Severity**: HIGH\n- **Solution**: Remove default values from compose file. Require explicit environment variables. Validate at startup (similar to the SECRET_KEY check in `config.py`).\n- **Priority**: 2\n\n---\n\n## SUMMARY: TOP 10 PRIORITY ITEMS\n\n| # | ID | Title | Severity | Owner |\n|---|-----|-------|----------|-------|\n| 1 | DO-01 | Docker Compose in production, no orchestration | CRITICAL | DevOps |\n| 1 | SA-01 | Single MongoDB instance SPOF | CRITICAL | DevOps |\n| 1 | DO-02 | MongoDB has no authentication | CRITICAL | DevOps |\n| 1 | DO-04 | No backup strategy | CRITICAL | DevOps |\n| 2 | SA-02 | Single Redis instance SPOF | CRITICAL | DevOps |\n| 2 | DO-03 | Secrets in env vars and defaults | HIGH | DevOps |\n| 2 | BE-01 | New MongoDB client per Celery task | HIGH | Backend |\n| 2 | DO-12 | MinIO default credentials | HIGH | DevOps |\n| 3 | SA-03 | No load balancer | HIGH | Architect |\n| 3 | SA-07 | No caching for detection control settings | HIGH | Backend |\n| 3 | BE-03 | No dead letter queue | HIGH | Backend |\n| 3 | DO-05 | No log aggregation | HIGH | DevOps |\n| 3 | DO-06 | No metrics or alerting | HIGH | DevOps |\n\n**Total findings**: 32 (10 Critical, 13 High, 8 Medium, 1 Low)\n\nThe most urgent items are the four CRITICAL findings that share priority 1: production deployment has no orchestration, MongoDB has no auth, there are no backups, and MongoDB is a single point of failure. These represent existential risks to the platform -- any one of them could cause total data loss or security breach in production."}],"stop_reason":"end_turn","stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2154,"cache_read_input_tokens":88603,"output_tokens":7491,"server_tool_use":{"web_search_requests":0,"web_fetch_requests":0},"service_tier":"standard","cache_creation":{"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":2154},"inference_geo":"","iterations":[],"speed":"standard"}},"requestId":"req_011CZJRhEPRzv1R2SUvYR7mb","type":"assistant","uuid":"3528fd09-a05f-469c-8dc1-86e75756a8c3","timestamp":"2026-03-22T16:25:15.238Z","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"C:\\Users\\jshah\\flooreye","sessionId":"31c38874-0fdd-46a7-87a9-fa414d8b993d","version":"2.1.81","gitBranch":"main","slug":"warm-exploring-rossum"}

{"parentUuid":"d5c9ef47-f005-4955-ab56-55ed7865f536","isSidechain":true,"agentId":"a04a981c06c41dbb0","message":{"model":"claude-opus-4-6","id":"msg_01P1sHMB8Ut9d8gcab6AsQuh","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"text","text":"I now have sufficient information to produce a thorough three-perspective audit. Let me compile the findings.\n\n---\n\n# FloorEye v2.0 Design Audit: Three Expert Perspectives\n\n## ROLE 4: DATABASE ENGINEER FINDINGS\n\n---\n\n### DB-01: Missing TTL Index on detection_logs Collection\n\n**Diagram(s):** ER_DIAGRAM, DATA_FLOW\n**Description:** The `detection_logs` collection is the highest-volume write target in the system (every frame inference produces a row), yet there is no TTL index and no archival strategy. The `system_logs` and `audit_logs` collections correctly have TTL indexes, but detection_logs will grow unbounded.\n**Root Cause:** TTL/archival was not included in the detection_logs index definition in `indexes.py`.\n**Impact:** Storage costs grow linearly forever. Query performance degrades as the collection grows past millions of documents. MongoDB memory-mapped indexes may not fit in RAM.\n**Severity:** Critical\n**Solution:** Add a TTL index on `detection_logs.timestamp` (e.g., 90 days), or implement a Celery-based archival job that moves old detection_logs to a cold-storage collection or S3 Parquet export. Add a config setting `DETECTION_LOG_RETENTION_DAYS`.\n**Priority:** 1\n\n---\n\n### DB-02: Unbounded Embedded Array in dry_references.frames\n\n**Diagram(s):** ER_DIAGRAM\n**Description:** The `DryReference` schema contains `frames: List[DryReferenceFrame]` where each frame includes `frame_base64` (a full Base64-encoded image). With 3-10 frames at ~100-500KB each Base64, a single document could reach 1.5-5MB, approaching MongoDB's 16MB document limit.\n**Root Cause:** Base64 frame data embedded directly in the document rather than stored in S3 with a path reference.\n**Impact:** Risk of hitting the 16MB BSON document size limit. Heavy reads/writes for what should be binary storage. Increased replication overhead.\n**Severity:** High\n**Solution:** Store dry reference frames in S3/MinIO (like detection frames already are), and replace `frame_base64` with `frame_s3_path` in the embedded array.\n**Priority:** 2\n\n---\n\n### DB-03: Missing Index on detection_logs.incident_id\n\n**Diagram(s):** ER_DIAGRAM, DATA_FLOW\n**Description:** The `list_detections()` service function in `detection_service.py` supports filtering by `incident_id` (line 197: `query[\"incident_id\"] = incident_id`), but there is no index on `detection_logs.incident_id` in `indexes.py`. This query is used to show all detections for an incident.\n**Root Cause:** Index was missed when the incident_id foreign key was added to detection_logs.\n**Impact:** Full collection scan on every \"show detections for incident\" query. Degrades as detection_logs grows.\n**Severity:** High\n**Solution:** Add `IndexModel([(\"incident_id\", ASCENDING)], sparse=True)` to the detection_logs index list in `indexes.py`.\n**Priority:** 2\n\n---\n\n### DB-04: Missing Index on detection_logs.model_source\n\n**Diagram(s):** ER_DIAGRAM\n**Description:** `list_detections()` supports filtering by `model_source` (line 200), but there is no index on this field.\n**Root Cause:** Index oversight.\n**Impact:** Collection scan when filtering detections by model source (common in ML pipeline workflows).\n**Severity:** Medium\n**Solution:** Add `IndexModel([(\"org_id\", ASCENDING), (\"model_source\", ASCENDING), (\"timestamp\", DESCENDING)])`.\n**Priority:** 5\n\n---\n\n### DB-05: No Cascade Delete / Orphan Prevention\n\n**Diagram(s):** ER_DIAGRAM\n**Description:** Deleting a store does not cascade to cameras, ROIs, dry_references, events, detection_logs, clips, devices, or edge_agents that reference it. Deleting a camera similarly orphans ROIs, dry_references, detection_logs, and events. No service implements cascade behavior.\n**Root Cause:** MongoDB has no built-in foreign key constraints. Application-level cascade was never implemented.\n**Impact:** Orphaned documents accumulate, consuming storage and potentially causing confusing UI states (e.g., cameras referencing deleted stores).\n**Severity:** High\n**Solution:** Implement cascade-delete service functions (or soft-delete with `is_active=False` propagation). Add a Celery periodic task to detect and clean orphaned documents.\n**Priority:** 3\n\n---\n\n### DB-06: No MongoDB Schema Validation\n\n**Diagram(s):** ER_DIAGRAM\n**Description:** No `jsonSchema` validators are defined at the MongoDB collection level. The only validation is Pydantic schemas on API input, but direct database writes (from Celery workers, edge agent uploads, migration scripts) bypass Pydantic entirely.\n**Root Cause:** Schema validation was never configured in MongoDB.\n**Impact:** Data integrity risk: malformed documents can be inserted by workers or internal services, leading to downstream failures.\n**Severity:** Medium\n**Solution:** Add MongoDB schema validation rules for critical collections (detection_logs, events, users) using `db.command(\"collMod\", ...)` in `ensure_indexes()`.\n**Priority:** 5\n\n---\n\n### DB-07: Missing Compound Index for events Query Pattern\n\n**Diagram(s):** ER_DIAGRAM, DATA_FLOW\n**Description:** The `list_incidents()` function queries with `org_id + store_id + status + severity + start_time` in various combinations, but the compound index only covers `(org_id, camera_id, status, start_time)`. A query filtering by `store_id + status` does not have an optimal index.\n**Root Cause:** Index design did not cover all common query patterns.\n**Impact:** Suboptimal query performance for store-filtered incident lists.\n**Severity:** Medium\n**Solution:** Add `IndexModel([(\"org_id\", ASCENDING), (\"store_id\", ASCENDING), (\"status\", ASCENDING), (\"start_time\", DESCENDING)])`.\n**Priority:** 4\n\n---\n\n### DB-08: camera.snapshot_base64 Stored Inline\n\n**Diagram(s):** ER_DIAGRAM\n**Description:** The `cameras` collection stores `snapshot_base64` directly in the document. A 1080p JPEG frame is ~200-500KB Base64-encoded. When listing cameras, if projection is not carefully managed, this field is fetched for every camera.\n**Root Cause:** Quick implementation stored snapshot inline rather than in S3.\n**Impact:** Camera list queries return unnecessarily large documents. Memory pressure on application servers.\n**Severity:** Medium\n**Solution:** Store snapshots in S3, replace with `snapshot_s3_path`. Ensure list queries exclude this field via projection.\n**Priority:** 5\n\n---\n\n### DB-09: Missing Sharding Strategy for High-Volume Collections\n\n**Diagram(s):** ER_DIAGRAM, DATA_FLOW\n**Description:** `detection_logs` and `events` are the highest-volume collections, receiving writes on every inference cycle. There is no documented or implemented sharding key strategy.\n**Root Cause:** Single-node deployment assumed during development.\n**Impact:** Vertical scaling limit. Cannot distribute write load across MongoDB shards when detection volume exceeds single-node capacity.\n**Severity:** Medium\n**Solution:** Document sharding strategy: `detection_logs` should shard on `{org_id: 1, timestamp: 1}` (hashed org_id for distribution + timestamp for range queries). Implement when scaling beyond single node.\n**Priority:** 7\n\n---\n\n### DB-10: MongoDB Production Deployment Without Authentication\n\n**Diagram(s):** ARCHITECTURE\n**Description:** The `docker-compose.prod.yml` file (line 44) explicitly states: \"MongoDB auth deferred to post-pilot.\" MongoDB is running without authentication in production.\n**Root Cause:** Deferred security hardening.\n**Impact:** Any process on the Docker network can read/write/drop all databases. Complete data breach risk if MongoDB port is exposed.\n**Severity:** Critical\n**Solution:** Enable `MONGO_INITDB_ROOT_USERNAME`/`MONGO_INITDB_ROOT_PASSWORD` immediately. Update `MONGODB_URI` with credentials. This is already partially configured in `config.py` but not enforced in Docker Compose.\n**Priority:** 1\n\n---\n\n### DB-11: Connection Pool Sizing Not Configured\n\n**Diagram(s):** ARCHITECTURE\n**Description:** The Motor/MongoDB connection is created with default pool settings. With 4 Gunicorn workers (production), each creates its own Motor client with the default pool size (~100 connections). That is 400 connections to MongoDB, which can overwhelm a small instance.\n**Root Cause:** No explicit `maxPoolSize` in the MongoDB URI or Motor client configuration.\n**Impact:** Connection exhaustion on MongoDB under load, especially with additional Celery workers.\n**Severity:** Medium\n**Solution:** Set `maxPoolSize=25` per worker in the MongoDB URI. Add `MONGODB_MAX_POOL_SIZE` to config.py.\n**Priority:** 4\n\n---\n\n### DB-12: training_jobs Collection Missing TTL/Archival\n\n**Diagram(s):** ER_DIAGRAM\n**Description:** Completed and failed training jobs accumulate forever with potentially large `config` embedded objects and log paths.\n**Root Cause:** No retention policy defined.\n**Impact:** Slow growth of unneeded data.\n**Severity:** Low\n**Solution:** Add a configurable retention period or archival to S3 for training_jobs older than 90 days.\n**Priority:** 8\n\n---\n\n## ROLE 5: SECURITY ENGINEER FINDINGS\n\n---\n\n### SEC-01: JWT Signing Key Shared Across All Token Types\n\n**Diagram(s):** ARCHITECTURE, DATA_FLOW\n**Description:** Both user JWT tokens and edge agent JWT tokens use HS256, but they use *different* secrets (`SECRET_KEY` vs `EDGE_SECRET_KEY`). However, there is no key rotation mechanism. If either key is compromised, all tokens of that type are compromised until the key is manually changed and all sessions/agents are invalidated.\n**Root Cause:** No key rotation strategy implemented.\n**Impact:** Long-lived edge tokens (180 days) are particularly dangerous -- a compromised edge token provides 6 months of access.\n**Severity:** High\n**Solution:** Implement key rotation: support `SECRET_KEY_PREVIOUS` for graceful rotation. Reduce edge token lifetime or implement token refresh for edge agents. Add a `/api/v1/edge/rotate-token` endpoint.\n**Priority:** 2\n\n---\n\n### SEC-02: WebSocket Auth Token in Query Parameter\n\n**Diagram(s):** DATA_FLOW, ARCHITECTURE\n**Description:** WebSocket authentication passes the JWT as `?token=<jwt>` in the URL query string (line 250 of `websockets.py`). Query parameters are logged in server access logs, proxy logs, browser history, and CDN logs.\n**Root Cause:** WebSocket API does not support custom headers during the upgrade handshake in browsers, so query params are the common workaround.\n**Impact:** JWT tokens leaked in logs, enabling session hijacking.\n**Severity:** High\n**Solution:** Use short-lived, single-use WebSocket ticket tokens: client requests a ticket via REST API (authenticated), then uses the ticket (valid for 30 seconds, single use) as the `?token=` parameter. Alternatively, send the token as the first WebSocket message after connection.\n**Priority:** 2\n\n---\n\n### SEC-03: MongoDB Running Without Authentication in Production\n\n**Diagram(s):** ARCHITECTURE\n**Description:** Same as DB-10. The production Docker Compose explicitly defers MongoDB authentication. This is a security finding in addition to a database finding.\n**Root Cause:** Deferred security hardening.\n**Impact:** Full database compromise if any network access to MongoDB port is possible.\n**Severity:** Critical\n**Solution:** Enable MongoDB authentication immediately.\n**Priority:** 1\n\n---\n\n### SEC-04: MinIO Default Credentials in Production\n\n**Diagram(s):** ARCHITECTURE\n**Description:** `docker-compose.prod.yml` lines 71-72 use `${MINIO_ROOT_USER:-minioadmin}` and `${MINIO_ROOT_PASSWORD:-minioadmin}` with insecure defaults. Config.py lines 56-57 also default to `minioadmin`. While `_INSECURE_DEFAULTS` checks exist for JWT and encryption keys, MinIO credentials are not checked.\n**Root Cause:** MinIO credentials not included in the production security gate in `config.py`.\n**Impact:** Full object storage access (all frames, models, clips) with default credentials.\n**Severity:** Critical\n**Solution:** Add `S3_ACCESS_KEY_ID` and `S3_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY` to `_INSECURE_DEFAULTS` check in `config.py`. Block production startup with default MinIO credentials.\n**Priority:** 1\n\n---\n\n### SEC-05: Rate Limiter Key Collision\n\n**Diagram(s):** ARCHITECTURE, DATA_FLOW\n**Description:** The rate limiter key (line 67 of `rate_limiter.py`) is `rl:{client_ip}:{path.split('/')[4]}`. This takes only the 5th path segment, meaning `/api/v1/stores/list` and `/api/v1/events/list` both produce key `rl:1.2.3.4:list`. Different endpoints share the same rate limit bucket.\n**Root Cause:** Overly simplified key derivation.\n**Impact:** Rate limiting is ineffective -- hitting one endpoint's limit blocks unrelated endpoints. Conversely, per-endpoint limits are not properly enforced.\n**Severity:** High\n**Solution:** Use the full matched prefix path as the key: `rl:{client_ip}:{path}` or at minimum the first 3-4 segments after `/api/v1/`.\n**Priority:** 2\n\n---\n\n### SEC-06: No CSRF Protection for Cookie-Based Auth\n\n**Diagram(s):** DATA_FLOW\n**Description:** Refresh tokens are stored in httpOnly cookies with `samesite=lax`. The refresh endpoint at `/api/v1/auth/refresh` presumably reads this cookie. With `samesite=lax`, GET requests from cross-origin navigation include the cookie. While POST-only endpoints are safer, there is no explicit CSRF token mechanism.\n**Root Cause:** Cookie-based refresh flow without CSRF defense-in-depth.\n**Impact:** Potential CSRF attacks on the refresh endpoint, though mitigated by SameSite=lax and POST-only.\n**Severity:** Medium\n**Solution:** Add a CSRF token header requirement for the refresh endpoint, or use the double-submit cookie pattern.\n**Priority:** 5\n\n---\n\n### SEC-07: Missing Security Headers\n\n**Diagram(s):** ARCHITECTURE\n**Description:** The FastAPI application does not set Content-Security-Policy, X-Content-Type-Options, X-Frame-Options, Strict-Transport-Security, or Permissions-Policy headers. The CORS middleware is present but no other security headers middleware exists.\n**Root Cause:** Security headers middleware was not implemented.\n**Impact:** Clickjacking, MIME-sniffing attacks, missing HSTS.\n**Severity:** Medium\n**Solution:** Add a middleware that sets: `X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff`, `X-Frame-Options: DENY`, `Strict-Transport-Security: max-age=31536000; includeSubDomains`, `Content-Security-Policy: default-src 'self'`, `Permissions-Policy: camera=(), microphone=()`.\n**Priority:** 3\n\n---\n\n### SEC-08: Edge Agent Token Never Validated Against token_hash\n\n**Diagram(s):** DATA_FLOW, ARCHITECTURE\n**Description:** In `edge.py` line 36-54, the `get_edge_agent` dependency decodes the JWT and looks up the agent by `id` from the JWT `sub` claim, but never validates the token against the `token_hash` stored in the `edge_agents` collection. If an edge agent is deprovisioned but the JWT has not expired, the agent still has access as long as the agent document exists.\n**Root Cause:** Token hash validation was stored but never checked.\n**Impact:** Revoked/rotated edge agent tokens remain valid until JWT expiration (180 days).\n**Severity:** High\n**Solution:** After finding the agent document, hash the presented token and compare against `token_hash`. Alternatively, add the agent's token JTI to a blacklist on deprovision.\n**Priority:** 2\n\n---\n\n### SEC-09: No Audit Trail for Edge Agent Actions\n\n**Diagram(s):** DATA_FLOW\n**Description:** Edge agents upload detections and frames via `/api/v1/edge/detection` and `/api/v1/edge/frame`, but these operations do not write to `audit_logs`. Only admin operations (provision, send-command) are audited.\n**Root Cause:** Edge agent endpoints were implemented without audit logging.\n**Impact:** No forensic trail if an edge agent is compromised and submits malicious detections.\n**Severity:** Medium\n**Solution:** Log edge agent uploads to `audit_logs` or at minimum to `system_logs` with the agent ID and payload metadata.\n**Priority:** 4\n\n---\n\n### SEC-10: store_access RBAC Not Enforced\n\n**Diagram(s):** ER_DIAGRAM, DATA_FLOW\n**Description:** Users have a `store_access: List[str]` field that should restrict which stores they can access. However, the `org_query()` filter only checks `org_id`. A viewer with access to Store A can query detections/incidents for Store B in the same org.\n**Root Cause:** `store_access` enforcement was defined in the schema but never implemented in query filters.\n**Impact:** Horizontal privilege escalation within an organization. Store owners see data from stores they should not access.\n**Severity:** High\n**Solution:** Add a `store_access_query()` helper that filters by both `org_id` and `store_id in user.store_access` when the user is not org_admin or super_admin.\n**Priority:** 2\n\n---\n\n### SEC-11: Encryption Key Stored in Environment Variable\n\n**Diagram(s):** ARCHITECTURE\n**Description:** The AES-256-GCM encryption key (`ENCRYPTION_KEY`) for camera credentials and integration configs is stored as a plaintext environment variable. It appears in `.env` files, Docker Compose `env_file` references, and potentially in process listings.\n**Root Cause:** No secrets management solution integrated.\n**Impact:** If the .env file or container environment is leaked, all encrypted data (camera credentials, integration configs) is compromised.\n**Severity:** Medium\n**Solution:** Integrate with a secrets manager (AWS Secrets Manager, HashiCorp Vault, or Docker Secrets). At minimum, mount the key from a file (`/app/secrets/encryption_key`) rather than environment variable.\n**Priority:** 5\n\n---\n\n### SEC-12: No Input Size Limits on Frame Upload\n\n**Diagram(s):** DATA_FLOW\n**Description:** Edge agents upload `frame_base64` and `detection_base64` via the edge API. There is no documented or enforced maximum payload size for these uploads. A malicious or compromised edge agent could upload arbitrarily large payloads.\n**Root Cause:** No request body size limit middleware.\n**Impact:** Denial of service via memory exhaustion on the backend.\n**Severity:** Medium\n**Solution:** Add a max request body size middleware (e.g., 10MB). Validate Base64 frame size before processing.\n**Priority:** 4\n\n---\n\n## ROLE 6: QA / TEST ENGINEER FINDINGS\n\n---\n\n### QA-01: Only 24 Tests Covering 95+ Endpoints\n\n**Diagram(s):** ARCHITECTURE\n**Description:** The test suite has 24 tests across 5 test files (test_auth, test_detection, test_detection_control, test_edge, test_integrations), but the system has 27+ routers with 95+ implemented endpoints. Test coverage is approximately 25%.\n**Root Cause:** Testing was added in a single session (Session 19) at the end of development.\n**Impact:** Most endpoints are untested. Regressions will go undetected. No confidence in refactoring.\n**Severity:** Critical\n**Solution:** Systematically add tests for every router. Prioritize: auth flows, incident lifecycle, notification dispatch, edge agent heartbeat/detection upload, camera CRUD, WebSocket connections.\n**Priority:** 1\n\n---\n\n### QA-02: No WebSocket Integration Tests\n\n**Diagram(s):** DATA_FLOW\n**Description:** The WebSocket hub (`websockets.py`) has 6 WebSocket endpoints handling real-time detection streaming, incident notifications, and edge status. None of these have tests.\n**Root Cause:** WebSocket testing requires special client setup (e.g., `httpx-ws` or `websockets` library) that was not configured.\n**Impact:** WebSocket authentication, channel routing, Redis pub/sub, and broadcast logic are entirely untested.\n**Severity:** High\n**Solution:** Add WebSocket tests using `httpx-ws` or Starlette's `TestClient` WebSocket support. Test: auth rejection, channel subscription, message broadcast, role enforcement.\n**Priority:** 2\n\n---\n\n### QA-03: No End-to-End Detection Pipeline Test\n\n**Diagram(s):** DATA_FLOW\n**Description:** The critical path (frame capture -> inference -> validation -> detection log -> incident creation -> notification dispatch -> WebSocket broadcast) spans 6+ services and is never tested end-to-end. Individual service tests exist but the integration is untested.\n**Root Cause:** End-to-end testing requires mocking camera streams, inference engines, and notification channels simultaneously.\n**Impact:** Integration bugs between services (data format mismatches, missing fields, race conditions) go undetected.\n**Severity:** High\n**Solution:** Create an e2e test that: inserts a camera, mocks the stream capture and inference, calls `run_manual_detection()`, and verifies the full chain (detection_log created, incident created, notification_deliveries queued, WebSocket message published).\n**Priority:** 2\n\n---\n\n### QA-04: No Edge Agent Testing Without Hardware\n\n**Diagram(s):** ARCHITECTURE, DATA_FLOW\n**Description:** The edge agent stack (Python agent, ONNX inference server, web dashboard) runs on physical hardware with cameras. There is no documented way to test edge functionality without real hardware. The edge agent's command polling, heartbeat, and detection upload flows are tested only via the backend API tests (5 tests in `test_edge.py`), not from the edge side.\n**Root Cause:** No edge agent simulator or mock camera feed system.\n**Impact:** Edge agent bugs (reconnection logic, buffer overflow, model hot-swap) cannot be caught in CI.\n**Severity:** High\n**Solution:** Create an edge agent simulator that generates synthetic frames, runs mock inference, and exercises the full edge-to-cloud flow. Add it to CI as a Docker Compose test target.\n**Priority:** 3\n\n---\n\n### QA-05: No Load/Performance Testing\n\n**Diagram(s):** ARCHITECTURE, DATA_FLOW\n**Description:** No load testing framework (Locust, k6, Artillery) is configured. The system's expected load (multiple edge agents sending detections every 0.5-2 seconds, concurrent WebSocket connections, concurrent API users) has never been tested.\n**Root Cause:** Load testing was not included in any phase.\n**Impact:** Unknown breaking point. The detection pipeline could bottleneck at MongoDB writes, Redis pub/sub, S3 uploads, or Celery task dispatch under real-world load.\n**Severity:** High\n**Solution:** Implement Locust or k6 load tests covering: concurrent detection uploads (100 agents x 2 fps), WebSocket connections (500 concurrent), API endpoint throughput, and MongoDB write saturation.\n**Priority:** 3\n\n---\n\n### QA-06: No Chaos/Resilience Testing\n\n**Diagram(s):** ARCHITECTURE\n**Description:** The system depends on MongoDB, Redis, S3/MinIO, and Celery. There is no testing for degraded operation when any of these fail. The rate limiter has a Redis fallback (in-memory), and the WebSocket broadcaster has a local-only fallback, but these are untested.\n**Root Cause:** No chaos engineering or failure injection testing.\n**Impact:** Unknown behavior during partial outages. The rate limiter fallback (line 91-107 of `rate_limiter.py`) silently drops to per-worker counting, which is less effective. WebSocket fallback loses cross-worker broadcast.\n**Severity:** Medium\n**Solution:** Add tests that: (1) disconnect Redis and verify rate limiter fallback, (2) disconnect MongoDB and verify graceful error responses, (3) disconnect Redis and verify WebSocket local-only mode. Use testcontainers or Docker health manipulation.\n**Priority:** 5\n\n---\n\n### QA-07: Test Database Does Not Run ensure_indexes\n\n**Diagram(s):** ARCHITECTURE\n**Description:** The `conftest.py` test database fixture creates a fresh Motor connection to `flooreye_test` but never calls `ensure_indexes()`. Tests run against a database without indexes, which means query performance issues and unique constraint violations are not caught in tests.\n**Root Cause:** `ensure_indexes()` is called in the app lifespan but not in test setup.\n**Impact:** Tests pass but production fails due to unique constraint violations. Index-dependent query behavior differs.\n**Severity:** Medium\n**Solution:** Add `await ensure_indexes(test_db)` to the `test_db` fixture after creating the connection.\n**Priority:** 3\n\n---\n\n### QA-08: Missing Contract Tests Between Frontend and Backend\n\n**Diagram(s):** ARCHITECTURE, DATA_FLOW\n**Description:** The React frontend and React Native mobile app consume the backend API, but there are no contract tests (e.g., Pact, OpenAPI schema validation) ensuring the frontend's TypeScript types match the backend's actual response shapes.\n**Root Cause:** No API contract testing strategy.\n**Impact:** Frontend breaks silently when backend response shapes change. TypeScript types drift from reality.\n**Severity:** Medium\n**Solution:** Generate TypeScript types from the FastAPI OpenAPI schema (`/api/v1/openapi.json`) using `openapi-typescript-codegen`. Add a CI step that regenerates types and fails if they differ from committed types.\n**Priority:** 4\n\n---\n\n### QA-09: No Staging Environment\n\n**Diagram(s):** ARCHITECTURE\n**Description:** Only development (docker-compose.dev.yml) and production (docker-compose.prod.yml) environments exist. There is no staging or pre-production environment for testing deployments before they reach the live system at `app.puddlewatch.com`.\n**Root Cause:** Infrastructure was set up for minimum viable deployment.\n**Impact:** Production is the first environment where Docker builds, migrations, and configuration are tested together.\n**Severity:** Medium\n**Solution:** Create a `docker-compose.staging.yml` deployed to a separate subdomain (`staging.puddlewatch.com`). Run the full test suite against staging before promoting to production.\n**Priority:** 5\n\n---\n\n### QA-10: No Notification Delivery Verification Tests\n\n**Diagram(s):** DATA_FLOW\n**Description:** The notification pipeline (rule matching -> quiet hours check -> deduplication -> Celery dispatch -> channel delivery) involves complex logic across `notification_service.py` and workers. There are no tests for: quiet hours enforcement, deduplication, circuit breaker behavior, FCM push delivery, or webhook delivery.\n**Root Cause:** Notification tests were not included in the test suite.\n**Impact:** Notification bugs (duplicate alerts, missed alerts during quiet hours, circuit breaker stuck open) will reach production undetected.\n**Severity:** High\n**Solution:** Add unit tests for: (1) quiet hours filtering, (2) deduplication window, (3) circuit breaker threshold, (4) dispatch lock window. Mock Celery tasks and FCM client.\n**Priority:** 2\n\n---\n\n### QA-11: Celery Worker Not Tested in CI\n\n**Diagram(s):** ARCHITECTURE\n**Description:** The Celery worker (`Dockerfile.worker`) runs notification delivery, training jobs, and other async tasks. CI only runs pytest against the FastAPI app. Celery task registration, serialization, and execution are not tested.\n**Root Cause:** CI does not start a Celery worker or Redis broker.\n**Impact:** Celery task signature changes, missing imports, or serialization errors are not caught until production.\n**Severity:** Medium\n**Solution:** Add a CI step that starts Redis (via service container), registers Celery tasks, and runs at least a smoke test calling `.delay()` and verifying task execution.\n**Priority:** 4\n\n---\n\n### QA-12: conftest.py Test Cleanup Races\n\n**Diagram(s):** N/A (test infrastructure)\n**Description:** In `conftest.py`, test cleanup (line 27-28) iterates all collections and calls `delete_many({})`. If tests run in parallel (pytest-asyncio with multiple workers), they will interfere with each other by deleting data mid-test.\n**Root Cause:** Shared test database without per-test isolation.\n**Impact:** Flaky tests in parallel execution.\n**Severity:** Low\n**Solution:** Use a unique database name per test (e.g., `flooreye_test_{uuid}`) or use transactions/sessions for isolation. Alternatively, enforce serial test execution.\n**Priority:** 7\n\n---\n\n## Summary by Severity\n\n| Severity | Count | IDs |\n|----------|-------|-----|\n| Critical | 4 | DB-01, DB-10, SEC-03, SEC-07, SEC-09, SEC-11, SEC-12, QA-06, QA-07, QA-08, QA-09, QA-11 |\n| Low | 2 | DB-12, QA-12 |\n\n## Top 5 Immediate Actions\n\n1. **Enable MongoDB authentication in production** (DB-10/SEC-03) --                     └──────────┘          └──────────┘\n```\n\n---\n\n## KEY ARCHITECTURAL OBSERVATIONS\n\n1. **Dual-path detection**: Edge does primary inference locally (ONNX Runtime), backend can also run manual detections (local ONNX or Roboflow API fallback).\n\n2. **Offline resilience**: Edge has its own SQLite incident database, local frame storage, and frame buffer. When cloud is unreachable, detections accumulate locally and sync when connectivity resumes.\n\n3. **Config propagation is bidirectional**: Cloud pushes directly to edge via Cloudflare tunnel (port 8091), and edge polls for commands as fallback. Heartbeat response includes config staleness checks for auto-healing.\n\n4. **WebSocket fan-out via Redis Pub/Sub**: Ensures broadcasts reach all Gunicorn workers. Six distinct channels scoped by org_id with role-based access control.\n\n5. **4-layer notification pipeline**: Notification rules matching -> quiet hours -> deduplication -> circuit breaker -> Celery async delivery with per-channel retry and exponential backoff.\n\n6. **IoT control spans cloud and edge**: Cloud triggers devices via HTTP/MQTT through the backend, while edge triggers devices directly on the local network (TP-Link TCP, MQTT, HTTP webhook) with auto-OFF timers.\n\n7. **S3 path convention**: Human-readable paths `frames/{org}/{store_name}/{camera_name}/{date}/{type}/` with sanitized names and local filesystem fallback.\n\n---\n\n**Files examined** (28 files total):\n- `C:\\Users\\jshah\\flooreye\\edge-agent\\agent\\main.py` (frame capture, heartbeat, camera loops)\n- automatic cascade deletion** in MongoDB. The codebase handles related cleanup manually in specific cases:\n\n- **dataset_frames deletion**: `dataset_service.py` explicitly deletes related `annotations` when a frame is deleted (`db.annotations.delete_many({\"frame_id\": frame_id})`)\n- **edge_agents deletion**: `edge_service.py` deletes related `edge_commands` (`db.edge_commands.delete_many({\"agent_id\": agent_id})`)\n- **ROI updates**: `camera_service.py` deactivates old ROIs (sets `is_active: False`) when creating new version -- soft delete pattern\n- **Dry reference updates**: Same soft-delete versioning pattern as ROIs\n- **token_blacklist**: Auto-expired via MongoDB TTL index on `expires_at`\n- **system_logs**: Auto-expired via TTL index (30 days)\n- **audit_logs**: Auto-expired via TTL index (365 days)\n- **All other deletions**: No cascading -- orphaned references remain (e.g., deleting a store does not auto-delete its cameras)\n\n---\n\n## MULTI-TENANCY PATTERN\n\nNearly every collection includes an `org_id` field for tenant isolation. DATA FLOW SUMMARY\n\n### Detection Flow (Edge-First)\n```\nCamera --RTSP--> Edge Agent --HTTP--> Inference Server (ONNX)\n                     |\n                     v\n              4-Layer Validation (local)\n                     |\n                     v\n              Redis Buffer (offline queue)\n                     |\n                     v\n              Uploader --HTTPS--> Cloud Backend --TCP--> MongoDB\n                                       |\n                                       v\n                                  Redis PubSub --WS--> Web/Mobile clients\n                                       |\n                                       v\n                                  Celery Worker --> Notifications\n                                       |\n                                  SMTP / FCM / Twilio / Webhook\n```\n\n### Command Flow (Cloud to Edge)\n```\nWeb UI --> Backend API --> MongoDB (edge_commands)\n                              |\nEdge Agent (polls /30s) <-----+\n     |\n     v\nExecute: deploy_model, reload_config, restart_camera, etc.\n```\n\n## 4. PORT MAP\n\n| Service | Port | Protocol | Binding |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| FastAPI Backend | 8000 | HTTP/WS | 0.0.0.0 |\n| MongoDB | 27017 | TCP (Wire) | 0.0.0.0 (dev), internal (prod) |\n| Redis (Cloud) | 6379 | TCP (RESP) | 0.0.0.0 (dev), internal (prod) |\n| MinIO API | 9000 | HTTP (S3) | internal |\n| MinIO Console | 9001 | HTTP | internal |\n| Nginx | 80 | HTTP | 0.0.0.0 |\n| Edge Inference Server | 8080 | HTTP | 127.0.0.1 only |\n| Edge Agent Web UI | 8090 | HTTP | 0.0.0.0 |\n| Edge Agent Config API | 8091 | HTTP | 0.0.0.0 |\n| Edge Redis Buffer | 6379 | TCP (RESP) | internal |\n| Web Dev Server (Vite) | 5173 | HTTP | dev only |\n\n## 5. KEY ARCHITECTURAL DECISIONS\n\n1. **Edge-first inference**: YOLO26 ONNX runs locally on edge GPU; cloud Roboflow is fallback only.\n2. **Redis triple-duty**: Cache/PubSub (DB0), Celery broker (DB1), Celery results (DB2) -- single Redis instance in cloud.\n3. **Separate edge Redis**: Independent Redis on edge for frame buffering with LRU eviction, survives cloud disconnection.\n4. **Cloudflare Tunnel both sides**: Cloud side tunnels public traffic in; edge side tunnels to Cloudflare for secure egress without open ports.\n5. **Polling not push for commands**: Edge agent polls backend every 30s for commands (no inbound ports needed).\n6. **Circuit breaker pattern**: All notification channels (SMTP, FCM, Twilio, webhook) have independent circuit breakers.\n7. **WebSocket via Redis PubSub**: Broadcasts work across multiple Gunicorn workers via PSUBSCRIBE on `ws:*` pattern.","is_error":false}]},"uuid":"0a3c3237-771c-4e20-92c6-d19bed094541","timestamp":"2026-03-22T16:23:17.299Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"905eb740-604e-4768-948b-049f1753d768","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"C:\\Users\\jshah\\flooreye","sessionId":"31c38874-0fdd-46a7-87a9-fa414d8b993d","version":"2.1.81","gitBranch":"main","slug":"warm-exploring-rossum"}
